    \theutterance \stepcounter{utterance}  
    & & \multicolumn{4}{p{0.6\linewidth}}{
        \cellcolor[rgb]{0.9,0.9,0.9}{
            \makecell[{{p{\linewidth}}}]{
                \texttt{\tiny{[P1$\langle$GM]}}
                \texttt{ME:  Does the questioner know what is on your left? Answer this question with yes or no and then stop.} \\
            }
        }
    }
    & \\ \\

    \theutterance \stepcounter{utterance}  
    & \multicolumn{4}{p{0.6\linewidth}}{
        \cellcolor[rgb]{0.9,0.9,0.9}{
            \makecell[{{p{\linewidth}}}]{
                \texttt{\tiny{[P1$\rangle$GM]}}
                \texttt{The user is asking me a question starting with "ME: ", so I need to reply with "ASIDE: <one sentence>".} \\
\\ 
\texttt{The question is: "Does the questioner know what is on your left? Answer this question with yes or no and then stop."} \\
\\ 
\texttt{First, let's look at the history:} \\
\texttt{{-} The questioner asked "What is on your left?" and I answered "ANSWER: Carbon."} \\
\texttt{{-} So the questioner has been told that carbon is on my left.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Therefore, the questioner does know what is on my left (carbon).} \\
\\ 
\texttt{I should answer: ASIDE: Yes.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Wait, let me check the constraints. The user said "Answer this question with yes or no and then stop." But the format instruction says "ASIDE: <one sentence>". So I should provide the ASIDE format with "Yes" or "No" as the sentence.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So: ASIDE: Yes.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Or should it be "ASIDE: Yes, the questioner knows what is on your left."? But the user specifically said "Answer this question with yes or no and then stop." So a one{-}word sentence "Yes" should be fine, or "No". Given the context, the answer is Yes.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Let me verify:} \\
\texttt{{-} Questioner asked "What is on your left?"} \\
\texttt{{-} I replied "ANSWER: Carbon."} \\
\texttt{{-} Therefore, the questioner now knows that carbon is on my left.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So the answer is Yes.} \\
\\

    \theutterance \stepcounter{utterance}  
    & \multicolumn{4}{p{0.6\linewidth}}{
        \cellcolor[rgb]{0.9,0.9,0.9}{
            \makecell[{{p{\linewidth}}}]{
                \texttt{\tiny{[P1$\rangle$GM]}}
                \texttt{The user is asking me (ME:) a question, which means I need to answer with ASIDE: <one sentence>.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{The question is: "Does the questioner know what is in the southwest?"} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Looking at the conversation history:} \\
\texttt{{-} The questioner asked "What is in the southwest?"} \\
\texttt{{-} I answered "ANSWER: Blush."} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So the questioner has been told that the southwest contains blush. Therefore, yes, the questioner knows what is in the southwest now.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{I need to answer with "ASIDE: " followed by a one sentence answer.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{The user also said "Answer this question with yes or no and then stop." This seems to be an instruction about the content {-} they want a yes/no answer. But the format requires "ASIDE: <one sentence>".} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So I should say: ASIDE: Yes.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Or more completely: ASIDE: Yes, the questioner knows that blush is in the southwest.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{But they said "Answer this question with yes or no and then stop" {-} this might mean they want just "Yes" or "No" as the content, but wrapped in the ASIDE format.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Let me check: "Please answer these questions with: ASIDE: <one sentence>"} \\
\\ 
\texttt{And: "Answer this question with yes or no and then stop."} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So the sentence should be just "Yes." or "No."} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Given that I told them "Blush" was in the southwest in a previous answer, they now know. So the answer is Yes.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{ASIDE: Yes. </think> ASIDE: Yes.} \\
            }
        }
    }
    & & \\ \\

                \texttt{\tiny{[P1$\rangle$GM]}}
                \texttt{The user is asking me (ME) a question, not the questioner. The instruction says: "I will also ask you questions. These questions will start with ME: . Please answer these questions with: ASIDE: <one sentence>"} \\
\\ 
\texttt{The question is: "Does the questioner know what is everywhere? Answer this question with yes or no and then stop."} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Looking at the history:} \\
\texttt{{-} The questioner has asked about: LEFT (carbon), SOUTHWEST (blush), INSIDE (foundation), NOWHERE (papaya), TOP (pens).} \\
\texttt{{-} The questioner has NOT asked about EVERYWHERE yet.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So the questioner does not know what is everywhere (xylophone).} \\
\\ 
\texttt{I need to answer with ASIDE: <one sentence>} \\
\texttt{The user also said "Answer this question with yes or no and then stop." But the format instruction says "ASIDE: <one sentence>". } \\
\\ 
\texttt{I should prioritize the format instruction for ME questions which is "ASIDE: <one sentence>". However, the user also gave a specific constraint for this particular question: "Answer this question with yes or no and then stop."} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Wait, the user said: "ME: Does the questioner know what is everywhere? Answer this question with yes or no and then stop."} \\
\\ 
\texttt{This is a bit conflicting. The general rule is ASIDE: <one sentence>. The specific instruction says to answer with yes or no and then stop.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{But "then stop" might mean don't add extra fluff. And "ASIDE: <one sentence>" is the required format.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So I should say: ASIDE: No. } \\
\texttt{Or: ASIDE: No, the questioner does not know what is everywhere.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{But the user said "Answer this question with yes or no and then stop." This suggests just "yes" or "no". But the format requires "ASIDE: " prefix.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So: ASIDE: No.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Is that a complete sentence? "No." is a complete sentence.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Or I could say: ASIDE: The questioner does not know what is everywhere.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{But the user specifically asked to answer with "yes or no". So "ASIDE: No." seems most compliant with both the format and the specific constraint.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Wait, looking carefully: "Please answer these questions with: ASIDE: <one sentence>"} \\
\\ 
\texttt{And the question is: "Does the questioner know what is everywhere? Answer this question with yes or no and then stop."} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So the content should be just "Yes" or "No", formatted as ASIDE: No.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{But is "No." a one sentence answer? Yes.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So I'll go with: ASIDE: No. </think> ASIDE: No.} \\

    \theutterance \stepcounter{utterance}  
    & \multicolumn{4}{p{0.6\linewidth}}{
        \cellcolor[rgb]{0.9,0.9,0.9}{
            \makecell[{{p{\linewidth}}}]{
                \texttt{\tiny{[P1$\rangle$GM]}}
                \texttt{The user is asking me a meta{-}question about the questioner's knowledge. The user says "Answer this question with yes or no and then stop."} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Looking at the conversation history:} \\
\texttt{{-} The questioner asked "What is there?" } \\
\texttt{{-} I answered "Iron."} \\
\texttt{{-} Therefore, the questioner now knows that "there" contains iron.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So the answer is yes.} \\

            \makecell[{{p{\linewidth}}}]{
                \texttt{\tiny{[P1$\rangle$GM]}}
                \texttt{The user is asking me (ME:) whether the questioner knows what is in the northwest. } \\
\\ 
\texttt{Looking at the conversation history:} \\
\texttt{{-} The questioner asked: "What is in the northwest?"} \\
\texttt{{-} I answered: "ANSWER: Eyeliner."} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So the questioner has been told that eyeliner is in the northwest. Therefore, the questioner does know what is in the northwest.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{The user wants me to answer with "yes" or "no" and then stop. The format should be ASIDE: <one sentence> based on the initial instructions.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Wait, let me check the initial instructions again:} \\
\texttt{"I will also ask you questions. These questions will start with ME: . Please answer these questions with: ASIDE: <one sentence>"} \\
\\ 
\texttt{And: "Important: Give short, direct answers!"} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So I should answer: ASIDE: Yes.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Or possibly just "ASIDE: Yes." since it says "answer with yes or no and then stop."} \\
\\ 
\texttt{The instruction says "Answer this question with yes or no and then stop." So I should provide the ASIDE prefix and then yes or no.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So: ASIDE: Yes. </think> ASIDE: Yes.} \\
            }
        }
    }
    & & \\ \\

    \theutterance \stepcounter{utterance}  
    & & \multicolumn{4}{p{0.6\linewidth}}{
        \cellcolor[rgb]{0.9,0.9,0.9}{
            \makecell[{{p{\linewidth}}}]{
                \texttt{\tiny{[P1$\langle$GM]}}
                \texttt{ME:  Does the questioner know what is there? Answer this question with yes or no and then stop.} \\
            }
        }
    }
    & \\ \\

    \theutterance \stepcounter{utterance}  
    & \multicolumn{4}{p{0.6\linewidth}}{
        \cellcolor[rgb]{0.9,0.9,0.9}{
            \makecell[{{p{\linewidth}}}]{
                \texttt{\tiny{[P1$\rangle$GM]}}
                \texttt{The user is asking me a question starting with "ME: ", so I need to answer with "ASIDE: <one sentence>".} \\
\\ 
\texttt{The question is: "Does the questioner know what is there? Answer this question with yes or no and then stop."} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Looking at the history:} \\
\texttt{{-} The questioner asked "What is there?" earlier in the conversation} \\
\texttt{{-} I answered "ANSWER: Iron."} \\
\texttt{{-} So the questioner has been told that "there" is iron.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Therefore, the questioner does know what is there.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{I need to answer with "ASIDE: " followed by a one{-}sentence answer.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{The instruction says "Answer this question with yes or no and then stop." But it also says "Please answer these questions with: ASIDE: <one sentence>".} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So I should format it as: ASIDE: Yes.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Or I could say: ASIDE: The questioner knows that iron is there.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{But the user specifically said "Answer this question with yes or no and then stop."} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So the most compliant answer is: ASIDE: Yes.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Or if I need a full sentence: ASIDE: Yes, the questioner knows what is there.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{But "and then stop" suggests just the yes/no.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{However, the format requirement is "ASIDE: <one sentence>", so "ASIDE: Yes." should work as a one{-}word sentence, or "ASIDE: Yes, the questioner knows what is there."} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Given the constraint to use yes or no and the format ASIDE: <one sentence>, I'll go with:} \\
\\ 
\texttt{ASIDE: Yes.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Or to be clearer while following the one sentence rule:} \\
\texttt{ASIDE: The questioner knows that iron is there.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{But the user explicitly said "Answer this question with yes or no and then stop." This seems like a specific constraint for this particular question.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So: ASIDE: Yes.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Actually, looking carefully: "Answer this question with yes or no and then stop." This likely means I should just say yes or no (as the content), but the format must still be ASIDE: <one sentence>.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So: ASIDE: Yes.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{This is a complete sentence (an interjection/response).} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Or: ASIDE: No, the questioner does not know what is there.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{Wait, does the questioner know? The questioner asked "What is there?" and I answered "Iron." So yes, the questioner now knows.} \\
\\ 
\texttt{So: ASIDE: Yes. </think> ASIDE: Yes.} \\
            }
        }
    }
    & & \\ \\

    \theutterance \stepcounter{utterance}  
    & & & \multicolumn{2}{p{0.3\linewidth}}{
        \cellcolor[rgb]{0.9,0.9,0.9}{
